If the process crashes or is killed mid-write, the governance.json file can be left in a partially-written (corrupted) state. The file already has corruption detection and backup logic in `loadGovernance()` (lines 44-51), which proves this scenario is considered plausible. The standard safe pattern is write-to-temp-then-rename (atomic on POSIX).

    24→  ```

    27→    return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, path.basename(`tasks-${teamId}.json`))  
    28→  }  
    29→  ```

A malicious ID would not match any team and return 404 before `docsFilePath` is reached. However, this is defense-by-coincidence, not defense-in-depth. ## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-19 18:24:02]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `task-registry.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/task-registry.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
    // Set timestamps based on status changes
    if ((updates.status === 'in_progress' || updates.status === 'review') && !tasks[index].startedAt) {
      tasks[index].startedAt = now
    }
    if (updates.status === 'completed' && !tasks[index].completedAt) {
      tasks[index].completedAt = now
    }

    // Clear timestamps when moving backward in workflow
    if (updates.status && updates.status !== 'completed') {
      tasks[index].completedAt = undefined
    }
    if (updates.status && (updates.status === 'backlog' || updates.status === 'pending')) {
      tasks[index].startedAt = undefined
    }
```

**New:**  
```
    // Clear timestamps first when moving backward in workflow
    if (updates.status && updates.status !== 'completed') {
      tasks[index].completedAt = undefined
    }
    if (updates.status && (updates.status === 'backlog' || updates.status === 'pending')) {
      tasks[index].startedAt = undefined
    }

    // Then set timestamps based on status changes (after clearing, so intent is unambiguous)
    if ((updates.status === 'in_progress' || updates.status === 'review') && !tasks[index].startedAt) {
      tasks[index].startedAt = now
    }
    if (updates.status === 'completed' && !tasks[index].completedAt) {
      tasks[index].completedAt = now
    }
```

**Result:**

<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `route.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**Old:**  
```
import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'
import { loadDocuments, createDocument } from '@/lib/document-registry'
import { getTeam } from '@/lib/team-registry'

// GET /api/teams/[id]/documents - List all documents for a team
export async function GET(
  _request: NextRequest,
  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }
) {
  const { id } = await params
  const team = getTeam(id)
  if (!team) {
    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team not found' }, { status: 404 })
  }
  const documents = loadDocuments(id)
  return NextResponse.json({ documents })
}

// POST /api/teams/[id]/documents - Create a new document
export async function POST(
  request: NextRequest,
  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }
) {
  try {
    const { id } = await params
    const team = getTeam(id)
    if (!team) {
      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team not found' }, { status: 404 })
    }

    const body = await request.json()
    const { title, content, pinned, tags } = body

    if (!title || typeof title !== 'string') {
      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'title is required' }, { status: 400 })
    }

    const document = await createDocument({
      teamId: id,
      title,
      content: content || '',
      pinned,
      tags,
    })

    return NextResponse.json({ document }, { status: 201 })
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Failed to create document:', error)
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to create document' },
      { status: 500 }
    )
  }
}
```

**New:**  
```

     1→# Code Correctness Report: api-governance  
     2→  
     3→**Agent:** epcp-code-correctness-agent  
     4→**Domain:** api-governance  
     5→**Files audited:** 6  
     6→**Date:** 2026-02-19T00:00:00Z  
     7→  
     8→## MUST-FIX  
     9→  
    10→_None found._  
    11→  
    12→## SHOULD-FIX  
    13→  
    14→### [CC-001] Missing UUID validation on `requestedBy` in transfers POST  
    15→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/governance/transfers/route.ts:52-68  
    16→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX  
    17→- **Category:** security  
    18→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    19→- **Description:** The `requestedBy` field is validated for authority (`isManager`/`isChiefOfStaffAnywhere`) but never validated for UUID format via `isValidUuid()`. While the authority check effectively rejects non-existent agents (since only registered agents can hold those roles), the `requestedBy` value is stored verbatim in the transfer request on disk. A non-UUID string (e.g., path traversal attempt or very long string) would be persisted even though the authority check would fail. However, if a valid manager/COS agent has a UUID as its ID (which they do since getAgent uses UUID), this is mitigated. The inconsistency with `agentId`/`fromTeamId`/`toTeamId` (all UUID-validated) is the concern.  
    20→- **Evidence:**  
    21→```typescript

    19→- **Description:** The `requestedBy` field is validated for authority (`isManager`/`isChiefOfStaffAnywhere`) but never validated for UUID format via `isValidUuid()`. While the authority check effectively rejects non-existent agents (since only registered agents can hold those roles), the `requestedBy` value is stored verbatim in the transfer request on disk. A non-UUID string (e.g., path traversal attempt or very long string) would be persisted even though the authority check would fail. However, if a valid manager/COS agent has a UUID as its ID (which they do since getAgent uses UUID), this is mitigated. The inconsistency with `agentId`/`fromTeamId`/`toTeamId` (all UUID-validated) is the concern.

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { checkMessageAllowed } from '@/lib/message-filter'  
     3→import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
     4→  
     5→// In-memory cache: avoids re-reading governance + teams files for every agent  
     6→// on each request. TTL of 5 seconds balances freshness with performance.  
     7→const cache = new Map<string, { ids: string[]; expiresAt: number }>()  
     8→const CACHE_TTL_MS = 5_000  
     9→  
    10→export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {  
    11→  try {  
    12→    const agentId = request.nextUrl.searchParams.get('agentId')  
    13→  
    14→    if (!agentId) {  
    15→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentId query parameter is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    16→    }  
    17→  
    18→    if (agentId && typeof agentId === 'string' && !/^[a-zA-Z0-9_-]+$/.test(agentId)) {  
    19→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid agentId format' }, { status: 400 })  
    20→    }  
    21→  
    22→    // Check cache first  
    23→    const cached = cache.get(agentId)  
    24→    if (cached && Date.now() < cached.expiresAt) {  
    25→      return NextResponse.json({ reachableAgentIds: cached.ids })  
    26→    }  
    27→  
    28→    // Cache miss or expired — compute reachable agents  
    29→    const allAgents = loadAgents()  
    30→    const reachableAgentIds: string[] = []  
    31→  
    32→    for (const agent of allAgents) {  
    33→      if (agent.id === agentId) continue  
    34→      if (agent.deletedAt) continue  
    35→  
    36→      const result = checkMessageAllowed({  
    37→        senderAgentId: agentId,  
    38→        recipientAgentId: agent.id,  
    39→      })  
    40→  
    41→      if (result.allowed) {  
    42→        reachableAgentIds.push(agent.id)  
    43→      }  
    44→    }  
    45→  
    46→    // Store in cache with TTL  
    47→    cache.set(agentId, { ids: reachableAgentIds, expiresAt: Date.now() + CACHE_TTL_MS })  
    48→  
    49→    // Evict stale/expired entries on every cache

    16→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX  
    17→- **Category:** race-condition  
    18→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    19→- **Description:** `saveGovernance()` calls `fs.writeFileSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE, ...)` directly. If the process crashes or is killed mid-write, the governance.json file can be left in a partially-written (corrupted) state. The file already has corruption detection and backup logic in `loadGovernance()` (lines 44-51), which proves this scenario is considered plausible. The standard safe pattern is write-to-temp-then-rename (atomic on POSIX).  
    20→- **Evidence:**  
    21→  ```typescript  
    22→  // line 63  
    23→  fs.writeFileSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE, JSON.stringify(config, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
    24→  ```  
    25→- **Fix:** Write to a temporary file in the same directory, then `fs.renameSync()` to the target path. This makes the write atomic. Note: this same pattern is missing in `lib/team-registry.ts:234` and `lib/transfer-registry.ts:45` (outside scope, but same issue).

    54→    }

**New:**

/** Write governance config to disk */
export function saveGovernance(config: GovernanceConfig): void {
  // Fail-fast: let errors propagate to callers (all wrapped in withLock try/catch)
  ensureAimaestroDir()
  // Phase 1: non-atomic write acceptable for single-process localhost.
  // Phase 2: use temp+rename for atomicity (write to tmp file, then fs.renameSync to target).
  fs.writeFileSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE, JSON.stringify(config, null, 2), 'utf-8')
```

    15→- **Description:** `buildAMPEnvelope()` assigns `message.content.type` directly to an `AMPPayload.type` field at line 98. However, `Message.content.type` (defined in `lib/messageQueue.ts:41`) is a union of 4 values: `'request' | 'response' | 'notification' | 'update'`. Meanwhile, `AMPPayload.type` (defined in `lib/types/amp.ts:165`) is a union of 10 values: `'request' | 'response' | 'notification' | 'alert' | 'task' | 'status' | 'handoff' | 'ack' | 'update' | 'system'`. This means:  
    16→  1. TypeScript will NOT flag an error because the 4-value union is assignable to the 10-value union (narrower to wider).  
    17→  2. However, if an AMP message arrives via `/api/v1/route` with `type: 'task'` or `type: 'alert'` and is stored into a `Message` object, the `Message.content.type` field will contain a value that its own type definition doesn't allow. This is a silent data integrity issue -- the received AMP payload type gets silently stored in a field that claims to only accept 4 values.

    10→### [CC-001] Type mismatch: Message.content.type (4 values) vs AMPPayload.type (10 values)  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/message-send.ts:98  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** type-safety  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `buildAMPEnvelope()` assigns `message.content.type` directly to an `AMPPayload.type` field at line 98. However, `Message.content.type` (defined in `lib/messageQueue.ts:41`) is a union of 4 values: `'request' | 'response' | 'notification' | 'update'`. Meanwhile, `AMPPayload.type` (defined in `lib/types/amp.ts:165`) is a union of 10 values: `'request' | 'response' | 'notification' | 'alert' | 'task' | 'status' | 'handoff' | 'ack' | 'update' | 'system'`. This means:  
    16→  1. TypeScript will NOT flag an error because the 4-value union is assignable to the 10-value union (narrower to wider).  
    17→  2. However, if an AMP message arrives via `/api/v1/route` with `type: 'task'` or `type: 'alert'` and is stored into a `Message` object, the `Message.content.type` field will contain a value that its own type definition doesn't allow. This is a silent data integrity issue -- the received AMP payload type gets silently stored in a field that claims to only accept 4 values.  
    18→- **Evidence:**  
    19→  ```typescript  
    20→  // lib/messageQueue.ts:40-42  
    21→  content: {  
    22→    type: 'request' | 'response' | 'notification' | 'update'  // 4 values  
    23→    ...  
    24→  }  
    25→  
    26→  // lib/types/amp.ts:165  
    27→  type: 'request' | 'response' | 'notification' | 'alert' | 'task' | 'status' | 'handoff' | 'ack' | 'update' | 'system'  // 10 values  
    28→  
    29→  // lib/message-send.ts:97-99  
    30→  const payload: AMPPayload = {  
    31→    t  

... [1663 more chars truncated]

    22→const LOCK_TIMEOUT = 5000 // 5 second timeout for acquiring lock  
    23→  
    24→/**  
    25→ * Acquire a lock for file operations  
    26→ */  
    27→async function acquireLock(): Promise<void> {  
    28→  if (!lockHeld) {  
    29→    lockHeld = true  
    30→    return  
    31→  }  
    32→  
    33→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
    34→    const timeout = setTimeout(() => {  
    35→      const index = lockQueue.findIndex(item => item.resolve === resolve)  
    36→      if (index !== -1) {  
    37→        lockQueue.splice(index, 1)  
    38→      }

    40→    }, LOCK_TIMEOUT)

    43→      resolve: () => {  
    44→        clearTimeout(timeout)  
    45→        resolve()  
    46→      },  
    47→      reject: (err: Error) => {  
    48→        clearTimeout(timeout)  
    49→        reject(err)  
    50→      },  
    51→    })  
    52→  })  
    53→}

    61→    if (next) {  
    62→      next.resolve()  
    63→    }

    // Block requests to hostnames that are not registered in the mesh network.
    const registeredHosts = getHosts()
    const targetHostname = parsedUrl.hostname.toLowerCase()
    const isRegisteredHost = registeredHosts.some(h => {
      try {
        const hostUrl = new URL(h.url)
        return hostUrl.hostname.toLowerCase() === targetHostname
      } catch {
        return false
      }
    })
    if (!isRegisteredHost) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Target host is not registered in hosts.json. Register the host before transferring agents.' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }

    // CC-016 fix: Redact agent ID from log to prevent info leakage in multi-user scenarios
    console.log(`[agent-transfer] Transfer initiated to ${parsedUrl.hostname}`)
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/agents/[id]/transfer/route.ts has been updated successfully.  

</details>

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * Simple in-memory rate limiter for governance password operations.  
     3→ * Tracks failed attempts per key with a fixed time window.  
     4→ * Phase 1 only — no distributed state needed for localhost.  
     5→ */  
     6→  
     7→const limits = new Map<string, { count: number; resetAt: number }>()  
     8→  
     9→const DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS = 5  
    10→const DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS = 60_000 // 1 minute  
    11→  
    12→/** Check if the rate limit allows another attempt */  
    13→export function checkRateLimit(  
    14→  key: string,  
    15→  maxAttempts: number = DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS,  
    16→  windowMs: number = DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS  
    17→): { allowed: boolean; retryAfterMs: number } {  
    18→  const now = Date.now()  
    19→  const entry = limits.get(key)  
    20→  
    21→  // Window expired — reset  
    22→  if (entry && now >= entry.resetAt) {  
    23→    limits.delete(key)  
    24→    return { allowed: true, retryAfterMs: 0 }  
    25→  }  
    26→  
    27→  // Check if over limit  
    28→  if (entry && entry.count >= maxAttempts) {  
    29→    return { allowed: false, retryAfterMs: entry.resetAt - now }  
    30→  }  
    31→  
    32→  return { allowed: true, retryAfterMs: 0 }  
    33→}  
    34→  
    35→/** Record a failed attempt */  
    36→export function recordFailure(key: string, windowMs: number = DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS): void {  
    37→  let entry = limits.get(key)  
    38→  const now = Date.now()  
    39→  // Reset expired windows so stale counts are not reused  
    40→  if (entry && now >= entry.resetAt) { entry = undefined; limits.delete(key) }  
    41→  const fresh = entry || { count: 0, resetAt: now + windowMs }  
    42→  limits.set(key, { count: fresh.count + 1, resetAt: fresh.resetAt })  
    43→}  
    44→  
    45→/** Reset rate limit on successful attempt */  
    46→export function resetRateLimit(key: string): void {  
    47→  limits.delete(key)  
    48→}  
    49→  
    50→// Periodic cleanup to prevent Map from growing unbounded  
    51→// (defensive — governance operations are infrequ

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→/**  
    13→ * LOCK ORDERING INVARIANT:  
    14→ * When acquiring multiple locks, always acquire in this order:  
    15→ *   1. 'teams'  
    16→ *   2. 'transfers'  
    17→ *   3. 'governance'  
    18→ * Violating this order will cause deadlock.  
    19→ *  
    20→ * Current nested lock usage:  
    21→ * - transfers/[id]/resolve/route.ts: acquires 'teams' then 'transfers' (via resolveTransferRequest)  
    22→ */  
    23→  
    24→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    25→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    26→// Set of currently held lock names  
    27→const held = new Set<string>()  
    28→  
    29→/**  
    30→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    31→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    32→ */  
    33→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    34→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    35→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    36→    held.add(name)  
    37→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    38→  }  
    39→  
    40→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    41→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    42→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    43→      locks.set(name, [])  
    44→    }  
    45→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    46→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    47→    })  
    48→  })  
    49→}  
    50→  
    51→/**  
    52→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    

... [894 more chars truncated]  

</details>

This is a silent data integrity issue -- the received AMP payload type gets silently stored in a field that claims to only accept 4 values.

    27→    return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, path.basename(`tasks-${teamId}.json`))  
    28→  }  
    29→  ```  
    30→- **Mitigating factor:** The API routes at `app/api/teams/[id]/documents/route.ts` call `getTeam(id)` first, which performs a lookup against the teams.json file. A malicious ID would not match any team and return 404 before `docsFilePath` is reached. However, this is defense-by-coincidence, not defense-in-depth.    127→/** Revert an approved/rejected transfer back to pending state.  
   128→ *  Used as a compensating action when a downstream operation (e.g. saveTeams)  
   129→ *  fails after the transfer was already marked as approved on disk. */  
   130→export async function revertTransferToPending(id: string): Promise<boolean> {  
   131→  return withLock('transfers', () => {  
   132→    const requests = loadTransfers()  
   133→    const idx = requests.findIndex(r => r.id === id)  
   134→    if (idx === -1) return false  
   135→  
   136→    requests[idx] = {

   139→      resolvedAt: undefined,

   141→      rejectReason: undefined,  
   142→    }

    15→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/governance/transfers/route.ts:52-68  
    16→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX  
    17→- **Category:** security  
    18→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    19→- **Description:** The `requestedBy` field is validated for authority (`isManager`/`isChiefOfStaffAnywhere`) but never validated for UUID format via `isValidUuid()`. While the authority check effectively rejects non-existent agents (since only registered agents can hold those roles), the `requestedBy` value is stored verbatim in the transfer request on disk. A non-UUID string (e.g., path traversal attempt or very long string) would be persisted even though the authority check would fail. However, if a valid manager/COS agent has a UUID as its ID (which they do since getAgent uses UUID), this is mitigated. The inconsistency with `agentId`/`fromTeamId`/`toTeamId` (all UUID-validated) is the concern.  
    20→- **Evidence:**  
    21→```typescript

    24→  return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid UUID format' }, { status: 400 })  
    25→}  
    26→// Line 68: requestedBy is NOT validated for UUID format  
    27→if (!isManager(requestedBy) && !isChiefOfStaffAnywhere(requestedBy)) {  
    28→```  
    29→- **Fix:** Add `!isValidUuid(requestedBy)` to the UUID validation check on line 62, or add a separate check before the authority verification.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-19 18:24:13]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `document-registry.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/document-registry.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
function docsFilePath(teamId: string): string {
  return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, `docs-${teamId}.json`)
}
```

**New:**  
```
function docsFilePath(teamId: string): string {
  // Validate teamId is a strict UUID to prevent path traversal (CC-001)
  if (!/^[0-9a-f]{8}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{12}$/i.test(teamId))
    throw new Error('Invalid team ID')
  // path.basename() as defense-in-depth against directory traversal
  return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, path.basename(`docs-${teamId}.json`))
}
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/document-registry.ts has been updated successfully.

    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/message-send.ts:98  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** type-safety  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `buildAMPEnvelope()` assigns `message.content.type` directly to an `AMPPayload.type` field at line 98. However, `Message.content.type` (defined in `lib/messageQueue.ts:41`) is a union of 4 values: `'request' | 'response' | 'notification' | 'update'`. Meanwhile, `AMPPayload.type` (defined in `lib/types/amp.ts:165`) is a union of 10 values: `'request' | 'response' | 'notification' | 'alert' | 'task' | 'status' | 'handoff' | 'ack' | 'update' | 'system'`. This means:  
    16→  1. TypeScript will NOT flag an error because the 4-value union is assignable to the 10-value union (narrower to wider).  
    17→  2. However, if an AMP message arrives via `/api/v1/route` with `type: 'task'` or `type: 'alert'` and is stored into a `Message` object, the `Message.content.type` field will contain a value that its own type definition doesn't allow. This is a silent data integrity issue -- the received AMP payload type gets silently stored in a field that claims to only accept 4 values.  
    18→- **Evidence:**  
    19→  ```typescript

    24→  }

    26→  // lib/types/amp.ts:165

**New:**  
```
  // ── Governance: Message Filter ──────────────────────────────────────
  // Always check governance regardless of sender resolution.
  // When sender is unresolved, pass null — checkMessageAllowed already handles
  // null senders (denies mesh-forward into closed teams).
  // When recipient is unresolved (both agentId and alias empty), deny by default
  // to prevent the literal 'unknown' from bypassing closed-team isolation.
  const recipientIdForFilter = toResolved.agentId || toResolved.alias
  if (!recipientIdForFilter) {
    throw new Error('Cannot send message: recipient could not be resolved to any known agent or alias')
  }
  const filterResult = checkMessageAllowed({
    senderAgentId: fromAgent?.agentId || null,
    recipientAgentId: recipientIdForFilter,
  })
  if (!filterResult.allowed) {
    throw new Error(filterResult.reason || 'Message blocked by team governance policy')
  }
```

**New:**  
```
  // ── Governance: Message Filter ──────────────────────────────────────
  // Always check governance for forwarded messages, consistent with sendFromUI().
  // Deny if recipient cannot be resolved to avoid 'unknown' bypass.
  const fwdRecipientIdForFilter = toResolved.agentId || toResolved.alias
  if (!fwdRecipientIdForFilter) {
    throw new Error('Cannot forward message: recipient could not be resolved to any known agent or alias')
  }
  const fwdFilterResult = checkMessageAllowed({
    senderAgentId: fromResolved.agentId || null,
    recipientAgentId: fwdRecipientIdForFilter,
  })
  if (!fwdFilterResult.allowed) {
    throw new Error(fwdFilterResult.reason || 'Message blocked by team governance policy')
  }
```
